         <!-- google_ad_section_start -->
         <h2 class="date-header">
          Thursday, December 31, 2009
         </h2>
         <div class="post hentry">
          <a name="1008636524445415615">
          </a>
          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/12/bring-it-on-2010.html">
            Bring It On, 2010!
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/Sz02zMcguzI/AAAAAAAAAS8/juk1SjSdqPU/s1600-h/New+Year.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5421549779565984562" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/Sz02zMcguzI/AAAAAAAAAS8/juk1SjSdqPU/s320/New+Year.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 150px; height: 113px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           It's been a rough year for a lot of people but in our home we've managed to maintain the status quo.  We're all healthy, employed and happy.  Glenn has a great job and the boys are doing very well in school.  I can't really ask for more so I'll just have to hope that 2010 brings more of the same.
           <br/>
           As far as my knitting goes, I never set goals for myself.  I make what I like making and it usually turns out the way it's supposed to.  Usually.  I have enough yarn in my stash to take me well into the new year so that makes me happy.  Doesn't take much really.  I'm a genuinely happy person.  I hope to do more socks this year and I see mittens in my boys future.  That's as far as I'll go for fortune telling for the coming year.
           <br/>
           Hope you all have a happy and healthy new year.
           <div style="clear: both;">
           </div>
          </div>

         <h2 class="date-header">
          Wednesday, December 30, 2009
         </h2>
         <div class="post hentry">
          <a name="8432376993172224000">
          </a>
          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/12/socks-snuggies.html">
            Socks &amp; Snuggies
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           Believe it or not, I actually have a new FO to show you!  Two in one week.  Whoda thunk it?
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/Szt5EWUGnbI/AAAAAAAAASs/kR5YfIJtbZM/s1600-h/Pink+Sock+1+Blog.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5421059692086861234" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/Szt5EWUGnbI/AAAAAAAAASs/kR5YfIJtbZM/s320/Pink+Sock+1+Blog.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 320px; height: 240px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/Szt5Qzdd7GI/AAAAAAAAAS0/u3-r-P9MY3o/s1600-h/Pink+Sock+2+Blog.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5421059906069195874" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/Szt5Qzdd7GI/AAAAAAAAAS0/u3-r-P9MY3o/s320/Pink+Sock+2+Blog.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 320px; height: 240px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           These are my
           <a href="http://www.islandofmisfitpatterns.com/2006/07/14/lacy-mock-cable-socks/">
            Lacy Mock Cable
           </a>
           socks.  Aren't they pretty?  They're knit with Artyarns Merino and were a fun knit. I finished them a couple of weeks ago but just haven't had a chance to photograph them and get them up.  I really like them but I'm having a problem.  I'm afraid to wash them because I'm scared they may felt.  I've washed them twice by hand so far but they didn't seem to come totally clean.  I'd love suggestions on how to wash them thoroughly without ruining them.
           <br/>
           What you see in the background, the leopard print, is my new Snuggie!  If you follow me on Twitter, you should know I was on a mad hunt for a leopard Snuggie.  After looking online and in several stores we finally found one in Walgreens.  Walgreens of all places!  So now we are the proud owners of a blue kids Snuggie, a pink adult Snuggie and the aforementioned leopard Snuggie.  I know they've become a national joke but I gotta tell you...when you sit and knit they sure come in handy!  I love my Tweeties.  Some suggested that I knit a Snuggie.  That'll be on next year's to do list.
           <br/>
           In other wonderful news, I heard from my niece a few weeks ago.  The same niece that's expecting a baby.  And she asked me to be her baby's Godmother!  I was so excited that I started crying.  Yes, I'm a big wuss and I admit it.  I think it's an honor to be asked and I'm very happy that she asked me.  Guess I better get my ass in gear and get the baby's gifts knitted up huh?  Well I ordered the yarn yesterday and I ordered it in a lovely light green so it will be good for either a boy or a girl.  I've had a premonition that she's having a boy but she thinks girl.  We'll see soon enough.
           <br/>
           Oh and for any of you that would love to buy Photoshop but don't happen to have an extra $700 laying around
           <a href="http://sixrevisions.com/graphics-design/10-excellent-open-source-and-free-alternatives-to-photoshop/">
            check this out
           </a>
           .  It's a list of Photoshop-like programs you can use to edit pictures.  I've been using Picnik and really like it.
           <br/>
           Hope you all have a most happy and healthy new year!
           <div style="clear: both;">
           </div>
          </div>

         <h2 class="date-header">
          Monday, December 28, 2009
         </h2>
         <div class="post hentry">
          <a name="8153901355885811152">
          </a>
          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/12/hands-up-baby-hands-up.html">
            Hands Up, Baby Hands Up.
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           Hope you all had as wonderful a holiday as we did.  We've been so busy and our home so full, I haven't had time to knit much or blog but I'm back now.
           <br/>
           Our sister in law came down with our nephew and the rest of her family to spend a day at Rockefeller Center and she was kind enough to leave her son here with us for a few days.  He's such a great kid and my boys just love him so it was a pleasure to have him here with us for a bit.  Then we had fifteen of us for Christmas Eve so that took some planning.  Now the kids are home for another week so I'll be busy keeping them occupied although the bikes they got for Christmas are keeping them out and about.
           <br/>
           I did get to finish something to show you.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SziFYY6smII/AAAAAAAAASk/UFepbxTQnWk/s1600-h/122709+005.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5420228805592389762" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SziFYY6smII/AAAAAAAAASk/UFepbxTQnWk/s320/122709+005.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 320px; height: 240px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           Glenn asked me to make him a pair of mittens so I did!  They were a breeze to do and they're my first pair of mittens! I'm not sure what pattern I used because I renamed it "Glenn's Mittens" when I downloaded it.  This is some of the yarn I bought from a guy off Craigslist so I don't know what kind of yarn it is.  It goes from thick to thin so and it can get very thick.  It's a bit difficult to work with because it's very ungiving but it made a lovely, thick, warm pair of mittens.
           <br/>
           Christmas morning was wonderful.  Megan sent me a gorgeous Namaste Binder bag which I had asked for this year.  It's red and I can't wait to get all my stuff into it.  She's a great gift giver and an even greater friend.  Glenn and the boys bought me a gorgeous red Laguna and Marilyn gave me a beautiful Namaste Buddy Case.  I should be a spokesperson for Namaste I have so much of their stuff!  Their products really are gorgeous, inexpensive and serve a great purpose for knitters.  I like that they're chic looking and can pass for a purse.  Granted a big one but a purse none the less.  I've always carried big bags with me so it's not a bother.  It sure deterred the mugger who tried to snatch my chain once but I digress.
           <br/>
           Marilyn also made me an absolutely gorgeous Ishbel which I so didn't expect.  She knits beautifully and, in the last year, has become a great friend.  I really wanted one of these and was planning on making myself one.  Eventually.  I'm glad Marilyn beat me to it.  It's got lace.  Gulp.
           <br/>
           Hope you're all enjoying your holiday season as much as I am!
           <div style="clear: both;">
           </div>
          </div>

         <h2 class="date-header">
          Tuesday, December 15, 2009
         </h2>
         <div class="post hentry">
          <a name="5449555768922489405">
          </a>
          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/12/i-finally-finished-something.html">
            I Finally Finished Something!
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           I was looking for something to make and realized that I didn't have a really warm hat to wear this winter.  I think that's the case with a lot of knitters.  We're so busy making for others, we forget ourselves.  I have my cool funky weed selling slouchy hat but I wanted something a little different.  I was looking through Ravelry and found the
           <a href="http://www.ravelry.com/patterns/library/flurries-slouch-hat">
            Flurries Slouch Hat
           </a>
           by Sandy Bingham and thought it was adorable and I had the perfect yarn for it!  I had the Cash Vero I'd gotten earlier this year at Wool Gathering and I knew it would make a lovely hat.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SyfEYh49eTI/AAAAAAAAASM/LuvjJ2CPYkQ/s1600-h/Striped+hat+003.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5415513002629495090" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SyfEYh49eTI/AAAAAAAAASM/LuvjJ2CPYkQ/s320/Striped+hat+003.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 320px; height: 240px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SyfEkM4SerI/AAAAAAAAASU/gSfGNAfHvUA/s1600-h/Striped+hat+005.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5415513203147963058" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SyfEkM4SerI/AAAAAAAAASU/gSfGNAfHvUA/s320/Striped+hat+005.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 320px; height: 240px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           Isn't it sweet?  It took me just one day to knit this up.  And, if you read here regularly, you know I'm all about the quick and easy.
           <br/>
           I'm just finishing up a pair of socks and then I'm going to be looking for more sock patterns I think.  I have oodles of sock yarn I'd like to start using so I'll be on a hunt for small projects.  I still have Pat's sweater to finish then I have to get the yarn for my niece's baby's set.
           <br/>
           Lots going on with the holidays coming as I'm sure is happening in most homes this time of year.  I love Amazon.  One stop shopping for gifts. And like I said, I'm all about the quick and easy.
           <div style="clear: both;">
           </div>

         <h2 class="date-header">
          Tuesday, December 8, 2009
         </h2>
         <div class="post hentry">
          <a name="5436752956411242552">
          </a>
          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/12/early-christmas.html">
            Early Christmas!
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           FedEx just came to the door with a present from Megan!  I thought I'd wait till Christmas to open it but nah.  It took all of .24 seconds for me to realize there is no way on God's green earth that I could wait another three weeks before opening this box so open it I did. And oh man am I happy I didn't wait.  It's more gorgeous than a photo could show so I will try to describe it to you.
           <br/>
           It's red and rectangular in shape.  It's hard on the outside which makes it really easy to zip open. It's got two zippers that open around and down so it can lay flat when opened.  Inside are three binder rings so I can round up all my patterns I've printed and get them in one place.  On both inside walls, there are zippered compartments.  There are four inserts: two zippered pouches and two needle holders.  I can also purchase other inserts for the bag if I need them! It really is just a beautiful bag that fills a niche I have.  I have needles, patterns and knitting tchotchkes that are all over the place which I can never find when I need them.  Now they will have a home.  A gorgeous, easily accessible home I might add.
           <div style="clear: both;">
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="post-footer">
           <div class="post-footer-line post-footer-line-1">

         <h2 class="date-header">
          Thursday, December 3, 2009
         </h2>
         <div class="post hentry">
          <a name="4042609648776268066">
          </a>
          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/12/back-to-knitting.html">
            Back To Knitting
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           I just looked back at my last few posts and realize there wasn't a whole helluva lot of knitting on my knitting blog. We now return you to your regularly scheduled knitting.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/Sxgrv2b-cYI/AAAAAAAAASE/cRRbrLm9E-0/s1600-h/Pink+%26+White+Sock+Picnik+2.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5411123053352350082" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/Sxgrv2b-cYI/AAAAAAAAASE/cRRbrLm9E-0/s320/Pink+%26+White+Sock+Picnik+2.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 320px; height: 240px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           Here's the beginning of my Lacy Mock Cable Sock.  I think I started these once before (if you really care, you can search my blog for it) but didn't like the yarn I was using for this pattern.  This yarn is just perfect for this pattern.  I just started this sock this morning and have been knitting on and off today but seem to have gotten quite a bit along on it.  For me anyway.
           <br/>
           This is Artyarns Ultramerino 4 color 128 which is a pink and white yarn which I got on the Ravelry Destash Group.  This is really a great group where you can find all different yarns to purchase for decent prices.  It's also a great group to join if you happen to run short of a yarn you need to finish a project.  You can put up an ISO (In Search Of) post and you may be able to find what you need.  The women are really nice and very helpful.  Some will even find the yarn you're looking for!
           <br/>
           All my knitted Christmas gifts are done.  I just have one knitted project that I started a long time ago that I have to finish.  That's right.  My sister's sweater.  I got it out of the closet today.  So far so good.  Al's coming over tomorrow and I'm hoping to get this thing finished with her help.  Maybe I can even get it done by Christmas.  Who am I kidding?  Her birthday's in August.  Let's shoot for that.
           <div style="clear: both;">
           </div>
          </div>

         <h2 class="date-header">
          Saturday, November 28, 2009
         </h2>
         <div class="post hentry">
          <a name="1933480497157847144">
          </a>
          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/11/tryptophan-kicked-my-butt.html">
            Tryptophan Kicked My Butt
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SxGejWu4UlI/AAAAAAAAARs/2Cgp_QRjNpg/s1600/Thanksgiving+Dinner.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5409278957683495506" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SxGejWu4UlI/AAAAAAAAARs/2Cgp_QRjNpg/s320/Thanksgiving+Dinner.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 320px; height: 240px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           Starting at 9 o'clock we have mashed turnips, sauteed mushrooms and onions, sweet potatoes, mashed potatoes with gravy and turkey topped with with brussel sprouts.  There's a glass of white wine on the side that didn't get into the photo.  I guess that didn't help my turkey hangover the next day.  I was a zombie and it's all the turkey's fault.  That's my story and I'm sticking to it.
           <br/>
           We had family and a friend over for dinner and it was a lovely day.  Lots of food and laughs and a few drinks.  What can be better?  Beautiful day so the boys were out playing all day and came home with voracious appetites.
           <br/>
           I've been working on my Christmas knitting and put in a request to my sistah from another mistah for my gift this year. The Namaste Binder:
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SxGgDvLdFJI/AAAAAAAAAR0/qTFI_cBQjJc/s1600/red.gif" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5409280613513237650" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SxGgDvLdFJI/AAAAAAAAAR0/qTFI_cBQjJc/s320/red.gif" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 320px; height: 173px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SxGgWOM9t4I/AAAAAAAAAR8/RG9aItU1OPU/s1600/photo6.gif" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5409280931078715266" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SxGgWOM9t4I/AAAAAAAAAR8/RG9aItU1OPU/s320/photo6.gif" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 320px; height: 173px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           How cool is that?  I carry all my needles around as it is so now they'll be organized in a gorgeous bag.  I just have to ask Santa for one more Laguna and I think my Namaste collection will be complete.  For now.
           <br/>
           Ok gotta get back to my Christmas knitting.  It'll be here before you know it!
           <div style="clear: both;">
           </div>

          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/11/happy-thanksgiving.html">
            Happy Thanksgiving
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/Sw5q-cCL_MI/AAAAAAAAARk/1pFWamOH3fg/s1600/rockwell-thanksgiving.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5408377823428345026" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/Sw5q-cCL_MI/AAAAAAAAARk/1pFWamOH3fg/s320/rockwell-thanksgiving.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 247px; height: 320px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           Today will be shared with friends and family here in our home.  During the course of the day I'll be thinking about all I have to be thankful for and that's quite a bit.  This is one of my favorite days of the year and the thing I'm most thankful for are the people I'll be spending it with.
           <br/>
           Happy Thanksgiving to you and yours.

         <h2 class="date-header">
          Monday, November 23, 2009
         </h2>
         <div class="post hentry">
          <a name="5542297053955536180">
          </a>
          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/11/presents.html">
            Presents!
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           I'm sorry I haven't been blogging lately but I don't really have much to say.  Yes I know that's a surprise but it's true.  I've been knitting some simple things for Christmas which I can't really post but I finally have something to show.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SwrIYM75iPI/AAAAAAAAARU/vMYLqcwlnyI/s1600/Neckwarmers.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5407354620726577394" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SwrIYM75iPI/AAAAAAAAARU/vMYLqcwlnyI/s320/Neckwarmers.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 320px; height: 240px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           These are
           <a href="http://disfordiana.wordpress.com/2009/06/28/something-new/">
            Birthday Cowls
           </a>
           I'm making for Patrick's teachers for holiday gifts. This is a great knit.  Not complicated but it looks like it is.  I have three done and three to go.  I really like this one:
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SwrIuUwpMnI/AAAAAAAAARc/dR6Zu4pOwtM/s1600/Neckwarmers+(1).jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5407355000783975026" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SwrIuUwpMnI/AAAAAAAAARc/dR6Zu4pOwtM/s320/Neckwarmers+(1).jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 320px; height: 240px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           I started it in gray thinking I had enough yarn.  Think again.  I had another yarn to finish it off and I really like the effect.  It's gray and white and looks a little snowflake like.  The last three rounds are done in gray again.  Very creative of me if I do say so myself.
           <br/>
           I have to finish the gifts then I'm going to dust off my sister's sweater and give it a go.  I'd love to get it to her by Christmas.  This Christmas.  We'll see  how it goes.
           <br/>
           Glenny's birthday is next week and he'll be fifteen.  Where does the time go?  So between Thanksgiving and his birthday, the time has been flying.
           <br/>
           Happy Thanksgiving to you and yours.  To those who don't celebrate Thanksgiving, Happy Thursday!
           <div style="clear: both;">
           </div>
          </div>

         <h2 class="date-header">
          Tuesday, November 17, 2009
         </h2>
         <div class="post hentry">
          <a name="4635968253524918636">
          </a>
          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/11/its-in-bag.html">
            It's In The Bag
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SwO-zgwFOhI/AAAAAAAAAQ0/OG5DZO0SXTw/s1600/Book.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5405373769948936722" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SwO-zgwFOhI/AAAAAAAAAQ0/OG5DZO0SXTw/s320/Book.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 86px; height: 114px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           No really.
           <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Its-Bag-Knitting-Projects-Take/dp/1592172482/ref=sr_1_4?ie=UTF8&amp;s=books&amp;qid=1258538068&amp;sr=8-4">
            It's In The Bag
           </a>
           is a new, and I have to say, wonderful book edited by
           <a href="http://www.sheknitsintheloop.com/">
            Kara Gott Warner
           </a>
           .  She's doing this really cool tour and I was lucky enough to be chosen to have my blog on her book tour.  Hollah!
           <br/>
           I got a copy of the book a few weeks ago and from the get go I really liked it.  As a newer knitter, I'm always looking for books that have projects that won't intimidate me and are fun knits.  This book has a lot of things I can actually make without a problem.  With sixty items to choose from, Kara covers all skill levels with ease.  Sixty?  Isn't that a lot for a book?  I thought so too!
           <br/>
           In it you'll find everything from place mats to belts, from a lovely woman's tank:
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SwPA7zuoF-I/AAAAAAAAAQ8/UDpZZ9gW0RQ/s1600/TakeItOnTheRoadTank.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5405376111505315810" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SwPA7zuoF-I/AAAAAAAAAQ8/UDpZZ9gW0RQ/s320/TakeItOnTheRoadTank.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 240px; height: 320px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           to a whole princess outfit for a little girl including a knitted crown!
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SwPBOvR3-_I/AAAAAAAAARE/xlN2uILqFE0/s1600/LittlePrincessDressUpSet.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5405376436728495090" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SwPBOvR3-_I/AAAAAAAAARE/xlN2uILqFE0/s320/LittlePrincessDressUpSet.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 240px; height: 320px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           Hmm...I wonder if I can get that crown to fit my head.  Maybe then my kids will believe I am the queen that I tell them I am.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           The book itself is really cool.  The photos are big and bright, the type is easy to read (some of us over forty folk will love to not have to find our reading glasses) and the instructions are really easy to follow.  This is one of those books that should be a staple in any knitters library because you'll go back to it again and again for patterns.  Someone having a baby?  There's a baby bunting, a onesie with a matching hat and a baby blanket.  A housewarming party?  Place mats, runners and a gorgeous earth tone afghan:
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SwPCtzxbtxI/AAAAAAAAARM/sj_-WTLXqBA/s1600/EarthTonesAfghan.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5405378070022174482" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SwPCtzxbtxI/AAAAAAAAARM/sj_-WTLXqBA/s320/EarthTonesAfghan.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 240px; height: 320px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           I wanted to review this book as a new knitter but I see that this book has so many really nice projects that it will grow with me.  As my skills develop, I will go back to this book again and again for more great knits.
           <br/>
           Make sure you stop by Kara's blog,
           <a href="http://www.sheknitsintheloop.com/">
            She Knits In The Loop
           </a>
           , to find other reviews of this book and to check out the great give aways she's doing on her blog.
           <div style="clear: both;">
           </div>
          </div>

          Friday, November 13, 2009
         </h2>
         <div class="post hentry">
          <a name="7483086197189202689">
          </a>
          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/11/i-won-again.html">
            I Won!  Again!
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           I like contests.  I love entering contest.  I really love winning contests.  Needless to say I was very happy to hear from Michele at
           <a href="http://pdxknitterati.com/">
            PDXKnitterati
           </a>
           that I'd won her contest!
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/Sv1fxtzwmFI/AAAAAAAAAQs/p6OvUA3cjNM/s1600-h/Contest+for+Blog.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">

           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           I won a lovely skein of Berroco Vintage Wool in a dark purple color along with a couple of sweet little handmade stitch markers. Thank's Michele!
           <br/>
           I've been reading Michele's blog for a while now and I really enjoy it.  She's a great knitter and a wonderful blogger.  Always something fun and informative on her blog.  Go take a look at her new clogs and see through sneakers!  Makes me almost want to buy some.  Almost.
           <br/>
           I'm working on some presents for Patch's teachers so I should actually have some knitting to show you soon.  Yes, photos of knitting on a knitting blog.  Whoda thunk it?

         <h2 class="date-header">
          Wednesday, November 11, 2009
         </h2>
         <div class="post hentry">
          <a name="5675028675422465503">
          </a>
          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/11/my-sweet-girl.html">
            My Sweet Girl
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/Svv98kS4anI/AAAAAAAAAQk/U05KIHd64ak/s1600-h/sickdog.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5403191394937891442" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/Svv98kS4anI/AAAAAAAAAQk/U05KIHd64ak/s320/sickdog.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 320px; height: 240px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SvtHce71xbI/AAAAAAAAAQc/GXj5T1cl7-s/s1600-h/Gracie+in+the+snow.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5402990732627002802" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SvtHce71xbI/AAAAAAAAAQc/GXj5T1cl7-s/s320/Gracie+in+the+snow.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 320px; height: 240px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           This is my sweet Gracie Girl.  We adopted her when she was just two months old.  The boys had always wanted a dog but we told them we wanted to wait till we had a house to get a dog.  The day we closed on our country house they asked when we were gonna get a dog.  The couldn't care less about they house, they just wanted the dog.  We wound up getting her about two months later.
           <br/>
           Since the day she came home she's been a part of our family.  We'd refer to her as the boys little sister.  She's sweet and good.  Quiet and loving.  Never a problem.  She sleeps in the living room, in her bed, but sneaks into the boy's bedroom at night because she thinks she's a kid too and the kids are there so she figures that's her place.
           <br/>
           About a week ago she started getting clingy.  She yelped once when Glenn was petting her but that's happened before because sometimes she eats something off the street when the boys walk her.  She started digging at her hind end so I called a vet in our neighborhood where Glenn took her today.  Apparently her anal glands were clogged and have now burst.  She's got two abscesses.  The doc gave her three shots, one antibacterial wash &amp; gel to be applied 2x a day and antibiotics.  I'm so upset that we didn't notice this.  Glenn's had dogs all his life and never had this issue so we didn't know what it was.  She's lying beside me now, a cone around her head and neck.  She's quiet and sleepy.  Hope she's gonna be ok.
           <div style="clear: both;">
           </div>
          </div>

I could kvetch about my damn knee which has kept me home for weeks on end but that gets old.  Fast.  I could blog about friends and family but there is no drama there, everyone's happy and healthy.
           <br/>
           Oh one thing I can show you is this:
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SvlZdAeJ6SI/AAAAAAAAAQU/2i0dG4VULfE/s1600-h/2-1.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">

         <h2 class="date-header">

         <div class="post hentry">

          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/11/wheres-knitting.html">
            Where's The Knitting?
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SvKxaVkHTeI/AAAAAAAAAP8/er1GSEl3Iss/s1600-h/singing+frog.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5400573969193979362" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SvKxaVkHTeI/AAAAAAAAAP8/er1GSEl3Iss/s400/singing+frog.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 116px; height: 95px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           That pretty well sums up my most recent knitting endeavors.  I've been knitting and frogging, knitting and frogging.  I think I've begun and ended three different things in the last couple of weeks.  Other than those fiascoes, I've knit a few repeat projects that don't really need to be blogged about.  Beanies, slippers and handwarmers which are easy tv knits.  Also I've been doing a few Christmas knits which I can't post about for obvious reasons.
           <br/>
           Oh and I think I'm getting senile.  I saw a pattern for a blanket a few weeks ago.  I now want to knit this blanket and it's not where I thought it was.  I can see it in my mind's eye but I have no frigging clue where I can find the pattern.  I'm going to go through every knitting book I have then cry then go to a Ravelry group for help.  Not necessarily in that order.
           <br/>
           Oh and how bout them Yankees?

         <h2 class="date-header">
          Tuesday, November 3, 2009
         </h2>
         <div class="post hentry">
          <a name="158379374278356421">
          </a>
          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/11/blog-pet-peeves.html">
            Blog Pet Peeves
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           I decided to write this in light of it being
           <a href="http://www.nablopomo.com/">
            NaBloPoMo
           </a>
           . These are a list of things I see on blogs that annoy me and I would please like you all to stop.  Now.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           1. If you do a food blog and post pictures, please look at these photos before posting them.  Grey meat is unappetizing as is coagulated cheese on top of aforementioned grey meat.
           <br/>
           2. Do not use the word orgasm or any of its synonyms when referring to food.  All I can picture is George Costanza in bed, screwing his girlfriend while eating a pastrami sandwich.  Again, not appetizing.
           <br/>
           3. If youre opening a can of Cambells anything, thats not homemade. Its Sandra Lee made.
           <br/>
           4. Supposably is not a word.  In any language.
           <br/>
           5. Use spell check.  Its free and easy.  Keep it employed.
           <br/>
           6. Dont be too wordy.  Read what youve written.  If you fall asleep at the keyboard, its too long.  Edit.
           <br/>
           7. If you must keep it long, make it entertaining.  People read for fun.
           <br/>
           8. If you cant make it entertaining make it educational.  I love to learn stuff while reading a blog.  Thats how I learned to knit!
           <br/>
           9. Please have your setting set to write black letters on white or light backgrounds.  White on black gives me googly eyes and Im sure Im not the only one.
           <br/>
           10.   Include pictures.  Oodles and oodles of pictures.  They dont have to be perfect but in focus would be nice.
           <br/>
           11.   Dont kvetch all the time.  Once in a while, a post of complaints is fine.  As readers we like to commiserate but more than once in a while, you need a therapist not a blog.
           <br/>
           12.   If talking about your children please dont call them the boy or the girl  If youre too freaked to use their real names give them fake ones or use their initials.  Calling them the child makes them sound like theyre foreign and not yours.
           <br/>
           13.   Have contests. Lots and lots of contests.  Mostly yarn giveaways but others will do fine too.
           <br/>
           14.   Dont put too many ads in the sidebars.  Its too distracting and makes me forget why I came to your blog.
           <br/>
           15.   Last but not least, have fun with it.  If youre not having fun writing it, believe me, were not having fun reading it.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           I hope youve enjoyed reading these.  And I hope I stick to my Do Not Do list.  I need to learn to practice what I preach.  I can promise no grey meat photos though!  Gag.

         <h2 class="date-header">
          Thursday, October 29, 2009
         </h2>
         <div class="post hentry">
          <a name="8542226044008079817">
          </a>
          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/10/tweeting-fine-yarns.html">
            Tweeting &amp; Fine Yarns
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           Hello.  My name is Susie and I'm a Tweetaholic.  I've been tweeting for a few months now and there's no end in sight.
           <br/>
           I joined Twitter a while ago and left the account dormant until recently.  I went on and followed a bunch of knitters, spinners and a few foodies.  At first I didn't see the point in this and now I can't get away from it.  It's so fun to see what everyone is knitting and talking about.  Pictures are posted of projects and people say nice things to one another for the most part.  I've been lucky enough to meet some other local knitters who I'm planning to knit with sometime in the foreseeable future and one I was lucky enough to meet yesterday!
           <br/>
           Al and I wanted to check out a new lys,
           <a href="http://gothamfineyarns.com">
            Gotham Fine Yarn
           </a>
           , and I asked a fellow Tweeter to join us!  Maria and I have been going back and forth commiserating on Twitter for a while now and I was really looking forward to meeting her.
           <br/>
           First Al and I went to Katz's for lunch.  Man there were a LOT of tourists.  A word of advice to anyone coming to visit NYC.  If you go to a deli, don't eat your pickles with a knife and fork and don't order a cheeseburger.  Those scream tourist.  Order either pastrami or, if adventurous, tongue and pick up the pickles with your hands.  That's your NYC lesson for today.  Ok then we went to Economy Candy which is stacked from floor to ceiling with all kinds of sweetness.  Then we went to:
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/Sumz-RsJfWI/AAAAAAAAAPs/g-TlirPn3v8/s1600-h/gfy_logo.gif" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5398043510862085474" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/Sumz-RsJfWI/AAAAAAAAAPs/g-TlirPn3v8/s320/gfy_logo.gif" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 175px; height: 175px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           Rebecca, the owner, is a delight.  She's sweet and smart and made us feel at home.  The store is stocked with beautiful Noro, Madeline Tosh and Ella Rae to name a few.  Needles and books are there too.  She's just opened but the store is by no means sparse.  Lots there and room to sit and knit!  Maria joined us and was a doll.  She fit right in with us and she and Rebecca even laughed at the song I sang them that my son made up.  I had so much fun that I screwed up my sock and have to frog it.  Again.  This will be the second time I rip it down and find another pattern.  I really need to pay attention to what I'm doing.  I just have too much fun sometimes.
           <br/>
           I'm hoping to get out to Brooklyn to meet up with Maria this weekend to do some more knitting.
           <br/>
           Please make sure you enter my contest below to win some delicious Progresso soup, a couple of cool mugs and spoons.
           <br/>
           Hopefully I'll have some knitting to show you next time.  But don't count on it.
           <div style="clear: both;">
           </div>
          </div>

         <h2 class="date-header">
          Wednesday, October 28, 2009
         </h2>
         <div class="post hentry">
          <a name="7144055803419744460">
          </a>
          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/10/more-yarn.html">
            More Yarn!
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           Saturday, the 17th was the first day of Rhinebeck.  I really didn't think I'd be able to go so I was sulking around the house.  Glenn suggested I get out to a yarn shop to cheer me up and cheer me up it did.  I couldn't grab my bag and wallet quick enough.  He was going to Brooklyn, so he dropped me and Patrick off down in the Financial District by
           <a href="http://www.seaportyarn.com/">
            Seaport Yarns
           </a>
           .  We get there and Andrea, the owner, was of course up at Rhinebeck but her lovely assistant, Lauren, helped us out.  She said she had a yarn that was dyed especially for them for Rhinebeck.  It was really pretty, rusty colors and a little dusky purple thrown in too.  I told Patrick to look around to see if he liked anything and he found a fun Jitterbug yarn.  Here they are:
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SugSvFpH4TI/AAAAAAAAAPk/6M0YQTFHBjk/s1600-h/Seaport+Yarns+005+For+Blog.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5397584753581351218" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SugSvFpH4TI/AAAAAAAAAPk/6M0YQTFHBjk/s320/Seaport+Yarns+005+For+Blog.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 320px; height: 240px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           The yarns were adorable and I can't wait to knit them up.  I was lucky enough, as you know, to be able to go to Rhinebeck the next day and buy more yarn.  I have a very patient, loving, generous and kind husband don't I?  He puts up with my crap and that should tell you A LOT!
           <br/>
           Today Al &amp; I are going to a new LYS here in Manhattan,
           <a href="http://gothamfineyarns.com">
            Gotham Yarns
           </a>
           .  It's down on the lower east side in one of my favorite neighborhoods.  So it's lunch at Katz's then knitting with friends.  Who could ask for more?  If you're in the area, stop in.  We'll be the loud ones.
           <div style="clear: both;">
           </div>
          </div>

          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/10/or-make-it-yourself.html">
            Or Make It Yourself
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           Does anyone remember those old Progresso Soup commercials?  Make it Progresso or make it yourself!  I'm doing a little contest.  One that is a bit unorthodox for a knitting blog but I thought it was cute.
           <br/>
           I'm a big soup person especially in the winter.  I was asked to do a giveaway on my blog for Progresso Soup through
           <a href="http://myblogspark.com">
            MyBlogSpark
           </a>
           !  Here's the deal and the prize.  Just tell me what your favorite soup is and I'll pick a winner in a week on Monday, November 2nd.  I'll send Progresso your information and they'll send you your prize which will be the following:
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SuYREceFQgI/AAAAAAAAAPc/WcEFyL8Sjds/s1600-h/Progresso.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5397019971509633538" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SuYREceFQgI/AAAAAAAAAPc/WcEFyL8Sjds/s320/Progresso.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 320px; height: 170px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           It's a can of High Fiber Chicken Tuscany soup, two large soup mugs and two spoons!  I got them all in the mail today and they're lovely mugs with a great can of soup.  The contest will end at midnight on Sunday and I'll post the winner on Monday.  Good luck!

         <div class="post hentry">
          <a name="7417039307288456369">
          </a>
          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/10/im-opinionated-too.html">
            I'm Opinionated Too
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           One of the first times I sat in a yarn shop to spend time knitting, Allyson and I were joined by another knitter.  I got frustrated with something and she said something along the lines of theres no crying in knitting.  She then went on to tell me about Elizabeth Zimmermann and her book Knitting Without Tears.  I eventually bought that book and The Opinionated Knitter.  Id skimmed through the latter, knowing that my knitting knowledge just isnt up to her patterns yet.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SuVoCvwqJiI/AAAAAAAAAPU/IlXMNZwJCxM/s1600-h/EZ.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5396834124862989858" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/SuVoCvwqJiI/AAAAAAAAAPU/IlXMNZwJCxM/s320/EZ.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 92px; height: 96px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           Glenn and I went to Coney Island to knit and metal detect at the crack of dawn today.  It was too cold for me so I went into the car and listened to
           <a href="http://fiberbeat.com/">
            WonderMikes Fiber Beat Podcast
           </a>
           .  He interviewed Meg Swansen and it was a delightful interview and piqued my interest in Elizabeth Zimmermann.  When I got home,  I picked up Opinionated Knitter to actually read it.  I know a bit more about knitting now than I did when I purchased the book so I wanted to give it a good going through and read her newsletters.
           <br/>
           The pictures of her sweaters, hats and gloves were lovely and, I have to admit, Im still a bit baffled by her patterns but I loved reading it.  I felt like I was a dear friend she was writing to in her newsletters and her writing about her camping with The Old Man.  I really enjoyed just getting to know her through her writing.  The pictures of her reminded me of my Granny who came from Scotland and passed away when I was only twelve.  She really touched me.  When I read the end, where Meg writes about her passing away, which I had already known about, I cried.  I felt like I was getting to know a new friend and then she was suddenly taken from me.
           <br/>
           Im sure there have been hundreds or even thousands of blog posts written about Elizabeth but I bet very few of them have nothing to do with knitting.  Im going to read more and learn more about Elizabeth and her way of knitting.  Not because shes so popular and everyone does it but because I really like her.  She makes me feel that even I, a novice knitter, can make the beautiful sweaters shes designed.  And one day, I will.
           <div style="clear: both;">
           </div>
          </div>

         <h2 class="date-header">
          Tuesday, October 20, 2009

         <div class="post hentry">

          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/10/100-things.html">
            100 Things
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           I wanted to put this up as a link at the top of my blog but can't figure it out.  I've had this list for months and just now decided to post it.  I figure it's now or never.  Here goes.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           100 Things About Me
           <br/>
           <br/>
           1. I think ice cream should be in the food pyramid.
           <br/>
           2. I've been married 22 years.  Nobody's dead.  Yet.
           <br/>
           3. I have two children both of the male gender.
           <br/>
           4. My mother died when I was 25.
           <br/>
           5. I hate to fly and have only done so twice.
           <br/>
           6. My older sister is 16 years older than me and more like a mother.
           <br/>
           7. I was born an aunt as my nephew is 2 years older than I am.
           <br/>
           8. I had 3 sisters but one died.
           <br/>
           9. I only knew my husband 5 months when we married.
           <br/>
           10. My eldest son was a baby model and on the cover of Child magazine.
           <br/>
           11. One of my sons looks just like me, the other just like my husband.  The one that didnt model, looks like me.
           <br/>
           12. I love to sing and I do a damn good job.
           <br/>
           13. My Kindle is my favorite gadget.
           <br/>
           14. I learned to knit as a child and hadn't done so for over 30
           <br/>
           years until last year.
           <br/>
           15. I'm a casual gamer and have a PlayStation Portable.
           <br/>
           16. I've lived in Manhattan most of my life, NYS all my life.
           <br/>
           17. I love to talk on the phone.
           <br/>
           18. I kick ass at Jeopardy.
           <br/>
           19. I think Chris Rock is a comedic genius.
           <br/>
           20. I get embarrassed for people on television, in awkward situations, and can't watch.
           <br/>
           21. I was an extra in the movie Fame.
           <br/>
           22. I'm a yarn ho.
           <br/>
           23. I'm very funny although this list isn't a good example.
           <br/>
           24. My best friend lives 1500 miles away and we've only met, in
           <br/>
           person, once.  Wah!
           <br/>
           25. I was Stumbling (Stumble Upon Firefox add on) and found a
           <br/>
           knitting blog that had socks.  This inspired me to start knitting
           <br/>
           again.
           <br/>
           26. I've met some great people at knitting shops.
           <br/>
           27. I'm agnostic.  Just in case.
           <br/>
           28. I've never been to The Statue of Liberty.  Or the Empire
           <br/>
           State Building.
           <br/>
           29. My sons think I'm a dork.  I tell them Im a cool mom.
           <br/>
           They dont believe me.
           <br/>
           30. I love anything lemon flavored.
           <br/>
           31. If I'd had a girl, her name would have been Colleen Bernadette.
           <br/>
           32. I miss my Dad more than words can say.
           <br/>
           33. I've learned that boys always laugh at farts.  Well into their
           <br/>
           forties.
           <br/>
           34. My current favorite restaurant is S'mac, a mac &amp; cheese
           <br/>
           restaurant here in the city.
           <br/>
           35. I love knitting outdoors.
           <br/>
           36. I'm a Harry Potter fan.  Big time.
           <br/>
           37. My favorite number is 3.  Third daughter, born on the third in
           <br/>
           sixty-three.  That's August 3rd in case you want to send presents.
           <br/>
           38. My husband makes me laugh, to the point of tears, at least once a day.
           <br/>
           39. I love Natalie Dees cartoons.
           <br/>
           40. I talk to my older sister at least twice a day on the phone.
           <br/>
           41. I like the country almost as much as the city.
           <br/>
           42. I'm fascinated by garden gnomes and have one guarding my
           <br/>
           country house.
           <br/>
           43. I have an herb garden.
           <br/>
           44. My name, Susan, means a lily as does my Hebrew name
           <br/>
           Shoshanna.
           <br/>
           45. I'd never won a contest until recently when I won some yarn!
           <br/>
           46. I can't sing in public unless I've had a few drinks.  Sometimes it takes more than a few.
           <br/>
           47. I cry at movies.  Even if they're only a little sad.
           <br/>
           48. I want to be cremated.  My husband doesn't.  He better live
           <br/>
           longer.
           <br/>
           49. I won't talk to celebrities when I see them out in public.
           <br/>
           50. I'm really angry that they cancelled Life On Mars.
           <br/>
           51. Love historic novels about Elizabeth I
           <br/>
           52. My dad was from Scotland.
           <br/>
           53. My mother was a native New Yorker.
           <br/>
           54. Top Chef is one of my favorite shows.
           <br/>
           55. My younger sister and I now have the best friendship we've ever had.
           <br/>
           56. I'd love to see Kathy Griffin perform.
           <br/>
           57. Pink is my favorite color.
           <br/>
           58. My husband got me a cabinet to store all my yarn.
           <br/>
           59. I love the sound of bagpipes.  May be genetic.
           <br/>
           60. Gracie, our lab/border collie, is the best dog. Ever.
           <br/>
           61. My mother was Jewish, my father, Catholic.  I have the
           <br/>
           market cornered on guilt.
           <br/>
           62. I hate that I can haz cheeseburger site.  With a passion.
           <br/>
           63. I laugh when people trip.
           <br/>
           64. I love old movies.  Especially ones with Cary Grant.
           <br/>
           65. I once went to the Thanksgiving Day Parade.  Never again.
           <br/>
           66. My husband is a better cook than I am.
           <br/>
           67. I love reading knitting blogs and have over two hundred
           <br/>
           bookmarked.
           <br/>
           68. I got my license when I was 36 and didnt start driving till I was 43.
           <br/>
           69. I usually wake up between four and five am.
           <br/>
           70. I started knitting a sweater for my sister and made a
           <br/>
           mistake.  I'm angry at it and it's in a bag in my closet and may
           <br/>
           reside there for another couple of months.
           <br/>
           71. My husband is the bravest man I know.  Except when it comes
           <br/>
           to flying insects.
           <br/>
           72. Watching The Real Housewives of NY is a guilty pleasure.
           <br/>
           73. I don't get the whole zombie thing.
           <br/>
           74. I love playing The Sims.
           <br/>
           75. My iPod is filled with disco.
           <br/>
           76. I waited on line, with both my boys, for over two hours to
           <br/>
           vote for Barack Obama.
           <br/>
           77. I think one of the secrets to a good marriage is laughter.
           <br/>
           78. I'm afraid to be at our country house alone.
           <br/>
           79. I cannot believe how much food a teenager can consume in
           <br/>
           one sitting.
           <br/>
           80. I never got to meet either of my grandfathers.
           <br/>
           81. I'm allergic to cats.
           <br/>
           82. I say I don't like people but I really do. I love to talk and
           <br/>
           laugh with others especially while knitting.
           <br/>
           83. Some of my favorite movies are How Green Was My Valley,
           <br/>
           The Quiet Man, The Right Stuff, Gladiator &amp; Braveheart.
           <br/>
           84. I lost one friend in the towers on 9/11.  I was lucky.
           <br/>
           85. My sister and brother in law own
           <a href="http://www.nyfirestore.com/index.html">
            NYC Original Firestore
           </a>
           in
           <br/>
           Greenwich Village.
           <br/>
           86. I love word games even though my best friend kicks my ass
           <br/>
           regularly at Wordscraper on Facebook.  I think she cheats.
           <br/>
           87. I have an awful memory and have started making lists for everything.
           <br/>
           88.  I love anything written by John Irving.  Especially Garp.
           <br/>
           89.  I found a cousin I never knew I had on Ancestry.com
           <br/>
           90.  I love to nap but I cant nap on my couch or I wake up angry.
           <br/>
           91.  I take great pride in my spaghetti sauce made from scratch.
           <br/>
           92.  It annoys me when people move to NYC for college, decide to stay and consider   themselves native New Yorkers.
           <br/>
           93.  I cant sleep comfortably unless my husband is sleeping beside me.
           <br/>
           94.  I could never get a pedicure from a man.  It creeps me out.
           <br/>
           95.  Chunky peanut butter is my favorite.
           <br/>
           96.  I work well under pressure.
           <br/>
           97.  I really wish my best friend lived closer.  I miss her being so far away.
           <br/>
           98.  Christmas is, by far, my favorite holiday.  Not bad for an agnostic, huh?
           <br/>
           99.  Im nearsighted and need glasses to drive.
           <br/>
           100. Damn. I really thought I was funnier than this.

         <h2 class="date-header">
          Monday, October 19, 2009
         </h2>
         <div class="post hentry">
          <a name="1476612622631290260">
          </a>
          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/10/knee-be-damned.html">
            Knee Be Damned
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           I know I've spoken about how great Glenn is and here is, yet again, another example of this.
           <br/>
           Sunday morning we woke up and the first thing he said to me was "Want me to take you to Rhinebeck, baby?"  I told him how I was afraid my knee wouldn't hold up and I don't like crowds blah blah blah.  He said we should go anyway and see how it feels and that, if need be, he'd push me around in a wheelchair.
           <br/>
           So we went.  Hollah!
           <br/>
           Glenn, Patrick and I went leaving the sullen, teeth sucking, eye rolling but generally good kid, Glenny, home alone because he had zero interest in going.  Boy did he miss out!
           <br/>
           We got there and it was pretty cold and damp but that was fine. We talked to some people at the gate who told us that it had been packed the day before and you could barely get into some of the buildings.  I was a little anxious about that but when we got in it was perfect.  Not crowded at all.  I don't know if that was because it was the second day or because of the weather.  We walked and shopped and watched llamas leap which was Patrick's favorite part.  The only disappointment was not being at the Ravelry get together. But I had the best companions in my husband and son and I wouldn't have had it any other way.  Here are pics
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/StwhrDwG8dI/AAAAAAAAAOs/KwUSAZUkMfc/s1600-h/Rhinebeck%2709+001.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5394223477308191186" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/StwhrDwG8dI/AAAAAAAAAOs/KwUSAZUkMfc/s320/Rhinebeck%2709+001.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 320px; height: 240px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           This was the sign on the way that Glenn insisted on photographing.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/StwiNgjvKvI/AAAAAAAAAO0/SBPhZBICRrQ/s1600-h/Rhinebeck%2709+002.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5394224069156481778" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/StwiNgjvKvI/AAAAAAAAAO0/SBPhZBICRrQ/s320/Rhinebeck%2709+002.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 320px; height: 240px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           Cool pumpkin carvings.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/StwidU_rosI/AAAAAAAAAO8/mXZXVw8ukxo/s1600-h/Rhinebeck%2709+005.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5394224340930372290" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/StwidU_rosI/AAAAAAAAAO8/mXZXVw8ukxo/s320/Rhinebeck%2709+005.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 320px; height: 240px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           Loot!
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/StwisJ-50uI/AAAAAAAAAPE/Jdg-GKW30Ok/s1600-h/Rhinebeck%2709+007.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5394224595672355554" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/StwisJ-50uI/AAAAAAAAAPE/Jdg-GKW30Ok/s320/Rhinebeck%2709+007.jpg" style="display:block; margin:0px auto 10px; text-align:center;cursor:pointer; cursor:hand;width: 320px; height: 240px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           <br/>
           Lovely basket.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           My loot consisted of three skeins of Socks That Rock, Aussi Sock, The Book of Yarn signed by the very sweet Clara Parkes and a lovely basket which I couldn't resist.
           <br/>
           The food was killer. Lamb sandwich, lamb &amp; barley soup and kielbasa was shared by all.  Glenn took an interest in the spinners and he and I are thinking of taking a class together!  All in all it was a great day for us all.  There was something there for everyone.  Even Glenny who got fudge out of the deal.  I can't wait till next year.  We're going to try to make it both days.
           <br/>
           Oh and my knee held up really well.  Good thing too.  Glenn said there was no way in hell he was gonna push me around in a wheelchair in the mud.  Ha!
           <div style="clear: both;">
           </div>

         <h2 class="date-header">
          Saturday, October 17, 2009
         </h2>
         <div class="post hentry">
          <a name="7666381607926235801">
          </a>
          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/10/rhinebeck.html">
            Rhinebeck
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           As you all know, the
           <a href="http://www.sheepandwool.com/">
            NY Sheep and Wool Festival
           </a>
           is taking place this weekend up in Rhinebeck NY.  Al has been telling me about it since she went last year and I haven't really had an interest in going.  Until now.
           <br/>
           Because of my knee and the facts that I don't like crowds or waiting in lines has made Rhinebeck not very appealing to me.  Of course, when I know I can't do something, it makes me want to do it more.  I've been on Twitter and everyone's Tweeting about it and I really want to go.  I've gotten to the point that I asked Glenn if he knew anyone with a wheelchair!  Talk about desperation.  Someone suggested that I go on Sunday because the crowds are smaller so that may be an option.  Today is the Ravelry meet up and I'm sorry not to be able to be there.  There are so many nice people on Ravelry who I've gotten to know through their posts and their blogs.  I'm sure everyone will have a ball today.
           <br/>
           If I don't go tomorrow, I'll just have something to look forward to for next year.  Maybe I'll hobble out to an LYS and buy something to make me feel better.
           <br/>
           Hope everyone there has a great time and buys lots of smooshy, delicious yarn!

         <h2 class="date-header">
          Wednesday, October 14, 2009
         </h2>
         <div class="post hentry">
          <a name="5617659401554720004">
          </a>
          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/10/me-and-my-baby-surprise-jacket.html">
            Me And My Baby Surprise Jacket
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           Theres a woman in my building having a baby and I wanted to make her something special.  Were friends and I wanted to make her something I hadnt made before but wanted to make for a long time.  The Baby Surprise Jacket.  Id seen these in every, and I do mean EVERY, knitting shop Id been in.  Al has made several.  Every place I go, I see people knitting this up so I was excited to give it a go.  Since my baby making days are over I kept an eye out for bulging bellies and an excuse to get this on my needles.
           <br/>
           I found out my friend was having a boy and began the hunt for a nice yarn for it.  I went to the Lion Brand Studio and picked up their Superwash in Sky.  A really nice merino yarn in a lovely blue color.  I purchased the book and I was ready to go.
           <br/>
           When I saw the instructions I was a little taken aback.  It wasnt the normal pattern, as Im sure you all know, and I was having a problem with it.  I really need a line by line pattern.  Its just the way my brain works.  Or doesnt work for that matter.  Im the kind of person who needs to see things.  If you describe a house to me, the way the rooms  are arranged, I cant see it in my minds eye.  I literally need it drawn out for me.  I felt this pattern was the same kind of thing, I needed it drawn out for me.  But I figured Id give it a go.
           <br/>
           It wasnt easy.  I even got the cheat sheet but still had a hard time with it.  People thought I was having a hard time because of the structure of the garment but no.  It was the actual pattern I just could not understand.
           <br/>
           Finally, after months of fits and starts, I got it done.  This is the one time I was happy that pregnancy was a nice long nine months.
           <br/>
           Everyone told me Oh wait till youre done.  Youll love it!  Guess what?  I dont.  I know this isnt the popular opinion to have but I just dont like it.  I mean its fine and all but for all the trouble I went through I just wasnt impressed.  This isnt to say that everyone will or should have the same feelings about it that I do but Im sure there are a few people ( Ill take even one person) who feel the same.  Maybe Im just not experienced enough to get it.  I dunno.  I just know that I felt that the amount of work and angst I put into it wasnt worth the outcome.
           <br/>
           Next friend that gets pregnant is getting a baby blanket.  A nice, plain, soft, square baby blanket.
           <div style="clear: both;">
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="post-footer">

             </a>

            <span class="post-icons">
             <span class="item-control blog-admin pid-562275690">

         <h2 class="date-header">
          Monday, October 12, 2009
         </h2>
         <div class="post hentry">
          <a name="1811809745080835935">
          </a>
          <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
           <a href="http://www.knittingknoobie.com/2009/10/brooklyn-rocks.html">
            Brooklyn Rocks!
           </a>
          </h3>
          <div class="post-header-line-1">
          </div>
          <div class="post-body entry-content">
           Because of the torn meniscus in my left knee, I've pretty much been housebound so it heals.  Well yesterday I broke out.  Glenn and I decided to go to Coney Island for a while.  He goes metal detecting on the beach and I sit on the boardwalk and knit.  The boys are old enough to leave home alone for a few hours, so we did just that.
           <br/>
           It was a beautiful day yesterday.  Sunny but cool.  Cool enough for me to wear my hand warmers!  It was so nice to be out of the house I think I'd have been happy if it had been nineteen degrees and snowing outside.  There were people walking and jogging up and down the boardwalk.  I was happy to just be there knitting.   Here's my sock in front of the landmark parachute jump at Coney Island.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/StLzgDXmz1I/AAAAAAAAAN0/oTyyGiG53Uk/s1600-h/Sock+at+Coney.JPG" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5391639435901587282" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/StLzgDXmz1I/AAAAAAAAAN0/oTyyGiG53Uk/s320/Sock+at+Coney.JPG" style="margin: 0px auto 10px; display: block; text-align: center; cursor: pointer; width: 300px; height: 225px;"/>
           </a>
           Then we got hungry and decided to grab a bite.  Glenn was nice enough to take me to my favorite breakfast (and dessert) place in the world:
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/StL0SbDYTPI/AAAAAAAAAN8/TWHOovaG6aI/s1600-h/Juniors+for+Blog.JPG" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5391640301252660466" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/StL0SbDYTPI/AAAAAAAAAN8/TWHOovaG6aI/s320/Juniors+for+Blog.JPG" style="margin: 0px auto 10px; display: block; text-align: center; cursor: pointer; width: 300px; height: 225px;"/>
           </a>
           Juniors!  Home of the most delicious cheesecake.  And their scrambled with lox and onions is fanfreakingtastic too.  We had a wonderful brunch and talked and laughed.  It was really nice to be away from the kids doing stuff we liked together.
           <br/>
           I told Glenn about the NYC Yarn Crawl and he asked me where there were knit shops in Brooklyn.  When I told him, he didn't hesitate in taking me there.  He is truly awesome.  So the first place we went to was
           <a href="http://www.brooklyngeneral.com/">
            Brooklyn General
           </a>
           .  There was a bench outside and Glenn asked if it was for the husbands.  The woman who worked there told Glenn there was a comfy couch in the back for him if he wanted to sit.  His theory is if you don't mind sitting in a yarn shop, you get the comfort of a couch.  He chose the couch.
           <br/>
           I was so happy to finally get to this store.  I'd heard a lot about it and it was gorgeous.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/StL1vFEB9yI/AAAAAAAAAOE/xSb5-C9ROAs/s1600-h/Brooklyn+General.JPG" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5391641893077645090" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/StL1vFEB9yI/AAAAAAAAAOE/xSb5-C9ROAs/s320/Brooklyn+General.JPG" style="margin: 0px auto 10px; display: block; text-align: center; cursor: pointer; width: 300px; height: 225px;"/>
           </a>
           <br/>
           They had a great variety of yarns and I could have spent all day there.  The woman working there was helpful and sweet.  I had a look around but didn't buy anything.  I'd love to go back when I have more time and my knee isn't bothering me.
           <br/>
           We then went to
           <a href="http://www.stitchtherapybrooklyn.com/">
            Stitch Therapy
           </a>
           , another shop in Brooklyn.  We met Kim there.  Hi Kim!  She has been going there for quite sometime and lives in the neighborhood.  This store was small but very well packed.  A nice variety of yarns and the young lady who worked there was helpful and very nice.  I understand they're moving to bigger digs.  Yay for them!  Again I didn't have something specific I wanted to buy, so I didn't purchase anything but I was really glad I was able to go and check this shop out.
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/StL30EAb2-I/AAAAAAAAAOM/Mv1Y5JAI0qU/s1600-h/Brooklyn+Stitch+Therapy.JPG" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5391644177716730850" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/StL30EAb2-I/AAAAAAAAAOM/Mv1Y5JAI0qU/s320/Brooklyn+Stitch+Therapy.JPG" style="margin: 0px auto 10px; display: block; text-align: center; cursor: pointer; width: 300px; height: 225px;"/>
           </a>
           I was having some pain at this point so we headed home.  I came home, put my leg up, whipped out my sock and watched a Bette Davis movie while knitting.
           <br/>
           You ever have one of those days that's just perfect?  Nothing special has happened but the person/people you're with are great and you're doing stuff you love.  I've had a few of those days in my life where I just say to myself "this is the perfect day".  Yesterday was one of those for me.  Great weather, doing fun things and really enjoying the company  I'm in.   Thanks to my wonderful husband I was able to have a day I'll never forget.  He rocks.
           <br/>
           Oh and a word of advice.  Don't knit with dpns on a boardwalk:
           <br/>
           <br/>
           <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/StL5vSiHrxI/AAAAAAAAAOU/eHhBq8XrJQ0/s1600-h/Boardwalk+for+Blog.JPG" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}">
            <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5391646294740021010" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_iKDtfKERnQY/StL5vSiHrxI/AAAAAAAAAOU/eHhBq8XrJQ0/s320/Boardwalk+for+Blog.JPG" style="margin: 0px auto 10px; display: block; text-align: center; cursor: pointer; width: 300px; height: 225px;"/>
           </a>
           Those cracks are a lot wider than you think.
           <div style="clear: both;">
           </div>
          </div>
